   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Panama Papers</h1>

     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Countries_implicated_in_the_Panama_Papers.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Countries_implicated_in_the_Panama_Papers.svg/450px-Countries_implicated_in_the_Panama_Papers.svg.png" width="450" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Countries_implicated_in_the_Panama_Papers.svg/675px-Countries_implicated_in_the_Panama_Papers.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Countries_implicated_in_the_Panama_Papers.svg/900px-Countries_implicated_in_the_Panama_Papers.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="443"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Countries_implicated_in_the_Panama_Papers.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Countries with politicians, public officials or close associates implicated in the leak on April 3, 2016
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <b>Panama Papers</b> are a <a href="/wiki/News_leak" title="News leak">leaked</a> set of 11.5&nbsp;million <a href="/wiki/Confidentiality" title="Confidentiality">confidential</a> documents that provide detailed information about more than 214,000 <a href="/wiki/Offshore_tax_haven" title="Offshore tax haven" class="mw-redirect">offshore</a> companies listed by the <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panamanian</a> corporate service provider <a href="/wiki/Mossack_Fonseca" title="Mossack Fonseca">Mossack Fonseca</a>, including the identities of shareholders and directors of the companies. The documents show how wealthy individuals, including public officials, hid their assets from public scrutiny. At the time of publication, the papers identified five then-heads of state or government leaders from <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> as well as government officials, close relatives, and close associates of various heads of government of more than forty other countries. The <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a> was home to half of the companies exposed and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> contained the most affiliated banks, law firms, and middlemen.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>While the use of offshore business entities is not illegal in the jurisdictions in which they are registered, during their investigation reporters found that some of the shell companies may have been used for illegal purposes, including fraud, drug trafficking, and tax evasion.<sup id="cite_ref-nuix_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nuix-2">[2]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>An anonymous source using the pseudonym "<a href="/wiki/John_Doe" title="John Doe">John Doe</a>" made the documents available in batches to German newspaper <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCddeutsche_Zeitung" title="Süddeutsche Zeitung">Süddeutsche Zeitung</a></span></i> beginning in early 2015. The information from this unremunerated <a href="/wiki/Whistleblower" title="Whistleblower">whistleblower</a><sup id="cite_ref-allyouneed_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allyouneed-3">[3]</a></sup> documents transactions as far back as the 1970s and eventually totaled 2.6 <a href="/wiki/Terabyte" title="Terabyte">terabytes</a> of data. Given the scale of the leak, the newspaper enlisted the help of the <a href="/wiki/International_Consortium_of_Investigative_Journalists" title="International Consortium of Investigative Journalists">International Consortium of Investigative Journalists</a> (ICIJ), which distributed the documents for investigation and analysis to some 400 journalists at 107 media organizations in 76 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The first news reports based on the papers, and 149 of the documents themselves, were published on April 3, 2016. The ICIJ plans to publish a full list of companies involved in early May 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Independent_Dearden_4_Apr_2016_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Independent_Dearden_4_Apr_2016-5">[5]</a></sup></p> 
     <p></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:20%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;"> 
      <div class="" style="background-color: #F9F9F9; color: black; text-align: center; font-size: larger; font-weight: bold;">
       From an internal leaked memorandum
      </div> 
      <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;"> 
       <div> 
        <p>Ninety-five per cent of our work coincidentally consists in selling vehicles to avoid taxes.</p> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">Partner of Mossack Fonseca<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian:_how_the_rich_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian:_how_the_rich-6">[6]</a></sup></cite>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Panama_City-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Panama_City-3.jpg/220px-Panama_City-3.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Panama_City-3.jpg/330px-Panama_City-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Panama_City-3.jpg/440px-Panama_City-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3992" data-file-height="2242"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Panama_City-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Panama City financial district
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>While no formal definition exists, a jurisdiction is typically considered an <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">offshore financial center</a>, sometimes less formally known as a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a>, when its banking infrastructure:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Primarily provides services to people or businesses who are not its residents.</li> 
      <li>Requires little or no disclosure of information when doing business.</li> 
      <li>Offers low taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-imfdef_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfdef-7">[7]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Customers in such a jurisdiction may require offshore accounts for any of a number of reasons, some entirely legal and ethically irreproachable;<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_explainer_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_explainer-8">[8]</a></sup> however, "the most obvious use of offshore financial centers is to avoid taxes", as journalists and researchers such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Tax_Justice_Network" title="Tax Justice Network">Tax Justice Network</a> have previously remarked.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">[10]</a></sup> Igor Angelini, head of <a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">Europol</a>'s <a href="/w/index.php?title=Financial_Intelligence_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Financial Intelligence Group (page does not exist)">Financial Intelligence Group</a>, said recently that the <a href="/wiki/Shell_companies" title="Shell companies" class="mw-redirect">shell companies</a> used for this purpose "play an important role in large-scale money laundering activities" and that they are often a means to "transfer bribe money".<sup id="cite_ref-firm_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firm-11">[11]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Law firms generally play a central role in offshore financial operations.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mossack_Fonseca" title="Mossack Fonseca">Mossack Fonseca</a>, the Panamanian law firm whose papers were leaked in the Panama papers affair, is one of the biggest in the business.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian:_how_the_rich_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian:_how_the_rich-6">[6]</a></sup> Its services to its clients include incorporating and operating shell companies in friendly jurisdictions on their behalf.<sup id="cite_ref-to_know_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to_know-12">[12]</a></sup> They can include creating "complex shell company structures" that, while legal, also allow the firm's clients "to operate behind an often impenetrable wall of secrecy".<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_explainer_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_explainer-8">[8]</a></sup> The leaked papers detail some of their intricate, multi-level, and multi-national corporate structures.<sup id="cite_ref-SSRN_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SSRN-13">[13]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Mossack Fonseca has acted on behalf of more than 300,000 companies, most of them registered in financial centers which are <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-to_know_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to_know-12">[12]</a></sup> The firm works with the world's biggest <a href="/wiki/Financial_institution" title="Financial institution">financial institutions</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale" title="Société Générale">Société Générale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse" title="Credit Suisse">Credit Suisse</a>, <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commerzbank" title="Commerzbank">Commerzbank</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nordea" title="Nordea">Nordea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gatekeeper_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gatekeeper-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-local-nordea_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-local-nordea-15">[15]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Tax_Justice_Network" title="Tax Justice Network">Tax Justice Network</a> called Panama one of the oldest and best-known tax havens in the Americas, and "the recipient of drugs money from Latin America, plus ample other sources of dirty money from the US and elsewhere", according to <a href="/wiki/The_Conversation_(website)" title="The Conversation (website)"><i>The Conversation</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ConversationPanama_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConversationPanama-16">[16]</a></sup> Panama has been cited repeatedly in recent years as a jurisdiction that does not cooperate with international tax transparency initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-ConversationPanama_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConversationPanama-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>International Monetary Fund (IMF) researchers estimated in July 2015 that profit shifting by multinational companies costs developing countries around US$213 billion a year, almost two percent of their national income.<sup id="cite_ref-imf_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf-21">[21]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Leak_timeline_and_logistics">Leak timeline and logistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Leak timeline and logistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Panama_papers_sz_chat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Panama_papers_sz_chat.jpg/220px-Panama_papers_sz_chat.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Panama_papers_sz_chat.jpg/330px-Panama_papers_sz_chat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Panama_papers_sz_chat.jpg/440px-Panama_papers_sz_chat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1320" data-file-height="743"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Panama_papers_sz_chat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A conversation between 
        <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCddeutsche_Zeitung" title="Süddeutsche Zeitung">Süddeutsche Zeitung</a></i> and 
        <a href="/wiki/Anonymous_source" title="Anonymous source" class="mw-redirect">anonymous source</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>More than a year before the April 2016 release of the leaked documents,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> an anonymous source who identified himself as "<a href="/wiki/John_Doe" title="John Doe">John Doe</a>" offered German newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCddeutsche_Zeitung" title="Süddeutsche Zeitung">Süddeutsche Zeitung</a></i> (SZ) large caches of sensitive banking documents. The newspaper accepted and in the space of a year received 2.6 <a href="/wiki/Terabyte" title="Terabyte">terabytes</a> of data made up of <a href="/wiki/Mossack_Fonseca" title="Mossack Fonseca">Mossack Fonseca</a> documents about<sup id="cite_ref-szabout_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szabout-23">[23]</a></sup> 214,488 offshore entities.<sup id="cite_ref-OCCRP_Giant_leak_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCCRP_Giant_leak-24">[24]</a></sup> The leaked documents numbered 11.5 million and were created between the 1970s and late-2015 by Mossack Fonseca.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian:_how_the_rich_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian:_how_the_rich-6">[6]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>At his insistence, reporters communicated with the source over encrypted channels only. Anonymity and an understanding that they would never meet face-to-face were his conditions for providing the documents. He said his life was in danger but declined remuneration.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC_anon_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_anon-26">[26]</a></sup> "There are a couple of conditions," he said. "My life is in danger, we will only chat over encrypted [lines]. No meeting ever."</p> 
     <p>According to <i>Süddeutsche Zeitung</i> reporter <a href="/wiki/Bastian_Obermayer" title="Bastian Obermayer">Bastian Obermayer</a>, the source said that he decided to leak the data because he thought that Mossack Fonseca acted unethically. "The source thinks that this law firm in Panama is doing real harm to the world, and the source wants to end that. That's one of the motivations," said Obermayer.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_anon_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_anon-26">[26]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Consortium_of_Investigative_Journalists" title="International Consortium of Investigative Journalists">International Consortium of Investigative Journalists</a> helped organize the research and document review once <i>Süddeutsche Zeitung</i> realized the scale of the work required to validate the authenticity of leak. Additional stories based on this data are in the works, and the full list of companies is to be released in early-May 2016. They enlisted reporters and resources from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/SonntagsZeitung" title="SonntagsZeitung" class="mw-redirect">SonntagsZeitung</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Falter" title="Falter">Falter</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/La_Naci%C3%B3n" title="La Nación">La Nación</a></i>, and German broadcasters <a href="/wiki/Norddeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Norddeutscher Rundfunk">NDR</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westdeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Westdeutscher Rundfunk">WDR</a>, and Austrian broadcaster <a href="/wiki/ORF_(broadcaster)" title="ORF (broadcaster)">ORF</a>, and eventually many others.</p> 
     <p>The sheer quantity of leaked data greatly exceeds the <a href="/wiki/United_States_diplomatic_cables_leak" title="United States diplomatic cables leak">Wikileaks Cablegate</a> leak in 2010<sup id="cite_ref-szabout_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szabout-23">[23]</a></sup> (1.7 <a href="/wiki/Gigabyte" title="Gigabyte">GB</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-DerFreitag_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DerFreitag-27">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Offshore_Leaks" title="Offshore Leaks" class="mw-redirect">Offshore Leaks</a> in 2013 (260 GB), the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Lux_Leaks" title="Lux Leaks" class="mw-redirect">Lux Leaks</a> (4 GB), and the 3.3 GB <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Leaks" title="Swiss Leaks">Swiss Leaks</a> of 2015. In comparison, the 2.6 TB of the Panama Papers equals 2,600 GB.</p> 
     <p>About 400 journalists from 107 media organizations in 80 countries at some point received and analyzed leak documents detailing the operations of the law firm and its clients' shell companies<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian:_how_the_rich_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian:_how_the_rich-6">[6]</a></sup> After more than a year of reporting, the first news stories based on the documents were published on 3 April 2016, along with 149 of the documents themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The data concerned the operations and workings of some 214,000 shell companies. Reporters sorted the documents into a huge file structure containing a folder for each shell company, which held the emails, contracts, transcripts, and <a href="/wiki/Image_scanner" title="Image scanner">scanned</a> documents Mossack Fonseca had generated while doing business with the company or administering it on a client's behalf.<sup id="cite_ref-szabout_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szabout-23">[23]</a></sup> Some 4.8 million leaked files were emails, 3 million were database format files,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> 2.2 million PDFs, 1.2 million images, 320,000 text files, and 2242 files in other formats.<sup id="cite_ref-szabout_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szabout-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Journalists indexed the documents, using <a href="/wiki/Open_software" title="Open software" class="mw-redirect">open software</a> packages <a href="/wiki/Apache_Solr" title="Apache Solr">Apache Solr</a> and Apache Tika,<sup id="cite_ref-forbes_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-30">[30]</a></sup> and accessed them by means of a custom interface built on top of Blacklight.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-30">[30]</a></sup> Süddeutsche Zeitung reporters also used <a href="/wiki/Nuix" title="Nuix">Nuix</a> for this, <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">proprietary software</a> donated by an Australian company also named <a href="/wiki/Nuix" title="Nuix">Nuix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nuix_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nuix-2">[2]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Using Nuix, SZ reporters also performed <a href="/wiki/Optical_character_recognition" title="Optical character recognition">optical character recognition</a> (OCR) processing on the millions of scanned documents, and the data they contained became both searchable and machine-readable. Most reporters then used Neo4J and Linkurious<sup id="cite_ref-forbes_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-30">[30]</a></sup> to extract individual and corporate names from the documents for analysis, but a few used Nuix for this as well.<sup id="cite_ref-nuix_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nuix-2">[2]</a></sup> They then cross-matched the compiled lists of people against the processed documents.<sup id="cite_ref-szabout_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szabout-23">[23]</a></sup> In the next step the reporters analyzed their information, trying to connect people, roles, monetary flow, and structure legality.<sup id="cite_ref-szabout_23-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szabout-23">[23]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_security">Data security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Data security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Mossack Fonseca notified its clients on 1 April 2016 that it had sustained an email hack. When the document leak became public, two days later, the firm dismissed any connection to the email hack, which it said had been limited in scope. Data security experts noted, however, that the company had not been encrypting its emails<sup id="cite_ref-forbes_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-30">[30]</a></sup> and furthermore seemed to have been running a three-year-old version of <a href="/wiki/Drupal" title="Drupal">Drupal</a> with several known vulnerabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-30">[30]</a></sup> Some <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.callowaygreen.co.uk/did-a-vulnerable-wordpress-plugin-bring-down-world-leaders/">reports</a> also suggest that some parts of the site may have been running <a href="/wiki/WordPress" title="WordPress">WordPress</a> with an out of date version of Revolution Slider, a plugin that has <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://blog.sucuri.net/2014/09/slider-revolution-plugin-critical-vulnerability-being-exploited.html">suffered</a> from vulnerabilities in the past.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_leak_and_leak_journalism">The leak and leak journalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The leak and leak journalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Gerard_Ryle" title="Gerard Ryle">Gerard Ryle</a>, director of the <a href="/wiki/International_Consortium_of_Investigative_Journalists" title="International Consortium of Investigative Journalists">International Consortium of Investigative Journalists</a>, called the leak "probably the biggest blow the offshore world has ever taken because of the extent of the documents."<sup id="cite_ref-BBC:_reveal_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_reveal-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a> described the release in a <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> message as the "biggest leak in the history of <a href="/wiki/Data_journalism" title="Data journalism">data journalism</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-TwittEdw_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TwittEdw-32">[32]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Panama-papers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Panama-papers.jpg/220px-Panama-papers.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Panama-papers.jpg/330px-Panama-papers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Panama-papers.jpg/440px-Panama-papers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="819"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Panama-papers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Panama Papers scandal illustrated
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>"This is a unique opportunity to test the effectiveness of <a href="/wiki/Leaktivism" title="Leaktivism">leaktivism</a>", said <a href="/wiki/Micah_M._White" title="Micah M. White">Micah White</a>, co-founder of <i><a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy</a></i>, "... the Panama Papers are being dissected via an unprecedented collaboration between hundreds of highly credible international journalists who have been working secretly for a year. This is the global professionalization of leaktivism. The days of WikiLeaks amateurism are over."<sup id="cite_ref-micah_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-micah-33">[33]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Icelandic investigative journalist and <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> spokesperson <a href="/wiki/Kristinn_Hrafnsson" title="Kristinn Hrafnsson">Kristinn Hrafnsson</a> has called for the Panama Papers to be published in full online. Hrafnsson, who worked on <a href="/wiki/Cablegate" title="Cablegate" class="mw-redirect">Cablegate</a> in 2010, said the withholding of documents is understandable to maximise the impact, but said that in the end the papers should be published in full for the public to access.<sup id="cite_ref-BelfastTelegraphWikiLeaks_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BelfastTelegraphWikiLeaks-34">[34]</a></sup> Hrafnsson's comments were reinforced by a <a href="/wiki/Twitter#Features.23Tweets" title="Twitter">tweet</a> from WikiLeaks which criticized the decision of the <a href="/wiki/International_Consortium_of_Investigative_Journalists" title="International Consortium of Investigative Journalists">ICIJ</a> to not allow full and transparent access to the Panama Papers, stating that, "If you censor more than 99% of the documents you are engaged in 1% journalism by definition."<sup id="cite_ref-carbonated.tv_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carbonated.tv-35">[35]</a></sup> WikiLeaks's position was, in turn, criticized, as the decision to disclose the documents at once would not have been the right one as far as "journalistic ethics" were concerned.<sup id="cite_ref-carbonated.tv_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carbonated.tv-35">[35]</a></sup> WikiLeaks also argued via a <a href="/wiki/Twitter#Features.23Tweets" title="Twitter">tweet</a> that the connection between the <a href="/wiki/International_Consortium_of_Investigative_Journalists" title="International Consortium of Investigative Journalists">International Consortium of Investigative Journalists</a> and the American government would undermine the integrity of the news leak;<sup id="cite_ref-carbonated.tv_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carbonated.tv-35">[35]</a></sup> this position was also, in turn, criticized as a theory which "Vladimir Putin would love."<sup id="cite_ref-carbonated.tv_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carbonated.tv-35">[35]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Clients_of_Mossack_Fonseca">Clients of Mossack Fonseca</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Clients of Mossack Fonseca">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_named_in_the_Panama_Papers" title="List of people named in the Panama Papers">List of people named in the Panama Papers</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Reports from 3 April noted financial and power connections to several high-ranking political figures and their relatives.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian:_how_the_rich_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian:_how_the_rich-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fusion:_Wikileaks_of_the_mega-rich_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fusion:_Wikileaks_of_the_mega-rich-37">[37]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Khalifa_Bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan-CROPPED.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Khalifa_Bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan-CROPPED.jpg/170px-Khalifa_Bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan-CROPPED.jpg" width="170" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Khalifa_Bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan-CROPPED.jpg/255px-Khalifa_Bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan-CROPPED.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Khalifa_Bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan-CROPPED.jpg/340px-Khalifa_Bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan-CROPPED.jpg 2x" data-file-width="383" data-file-height="484"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Khalifa_Bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan-CROPPED.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> United Arab Emirates President 
        <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Several national leaders were named, including presidents <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a> of the United Arab Emirates, <a href="/wiki/Petro_Poroshenko" title="Petro Poroshenko">Petro Poroshenko</a> of Ukraine, King <a href="/wiki/Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Salman of Saudi Arabia">Salman of Saudi Arabia</a>, as well as the Prime Minister of Iceland, <a href="/wiki/Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugsson" title="Sigmundur Davíð Gunnlaugsson">Sigmundur Davíð Gunnlaugsson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup> Former heads of state mentioned in the papers include Sudanese president <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_al-Mirghani" title="Ahmed al-Mirghani">Ahmed al-Mirghani</a>, the Emir of Qatar <a href="/wiki/Hamad_bin_Khalifa_Al_Thani" title="Hamad bin Khalifa Al Thani">Hamad bin Khalifa Al Thani</a>, and prime ministers of Georgia <a href="/wiki/Bidzina_Ivanishvili" title="Bidzina Ivanishvili">Bidzina Ivanishvili</a>, Iraq <a href="/wiki/Ayad_Allawi" title="Ayad Allawi">Ayad Allawi</a>, and Jordan <a href="/wiki/Ali_Abu_al-Ragheb" title="Ali Abu al-Ragheb">Ali Abu al-Ragheb</a>, former Prime Minister of <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> <a href="/wiki/Hamad_bin_Jassim_bin_Jaber_Al_Thani" title="Hamad bin Jassim bin Jaber Al Thani">Hamad bin Jassim bin Jaber Al Thani</a>, former Ukrainian prime minister <a href="/wiki/Pavlo_Lazarenko" title="Pavlo Lazarenko">Pavlo Lazarenko</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup> and former prime minister of <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a> <a href="/wiki/Ion_Sturza" title="Ion Sturza">Ion Sturza</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The leaked files identified 61 family members and associates of prime ministers, presidents and kings,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> including the deceased father of British prime minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, the brother-in-law of China's <a href="/wiki/Paramount_leader" title="Paramount leader">paramount leader</a> <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup> the son of <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Malaysia" title="Prime Minister of Malaysia">Malaysian prime minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Najib_Razak" title="Najib Razak">Najib Razak</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup> the children of <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Pakistan" title="Prime Minister of Pakistan">Pakistani prime minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Nawaz_Sharif" title="Nawaz Sharif">Nawaz Sharif</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijani</a> president <a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">Ilham Aliyev</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Khulubuse_Zuma" title="Khulubuse Zuma">Clive Khulubuse Zuma</a>, the nephew of <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South African</a> president <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Zuma" title="Jacob Zuma">Jacob Zuma</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CICJZuma_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CICJZuma-40">[40]</a></sup> the grandson of <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakh</a> president <a href="/wiki/Nursultan_Nazarbayev" title="Nursultan Nazarbayev">Nursultan Nazarbayev</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup> the personal secretary of <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Morocco" title="List of rulers of Morocco">Moroccan king</a> <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_VI_of_Morocco" title="Mohammed VI of Morocco">Mohammed VI</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup> and the "favourite contractor" of <a href="/wiki/President_of_Mexico" title="President of Mexico">Mexican president</a> <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto" title="Enrique Peña Nieto">Enrique Peña Nieto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Other clients included less senior government officials and their close relatives and associates from over forty different countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Many individuals mentioned in the Panama Papers were connected with the world governing body of association football, <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, including former president of <a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">CONMEBOL</a> <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Figueredo" title="Eugenio Figueredo">Eugenio Figueredo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian:_FIFA_Ethics_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian:_FIFA_Ethics-41">[41]</a></sup> former <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_UEFA" title="List of Presidents of UEFA">President of UEFA</a> <a href="/wiki/Michel_Platini" title="Michel Platini">Michel Platini</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FusionFIFAApr316_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FusionFIFAApr316-42">[42]</a></sup> former secretary general of FIFA <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_Valcke" title="Jérôme Valcke">Jérôme Valcke</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FusionFIFAApr316_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FusionFIFAApr316-42">[42]</a></sup> Argentine player <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a>, and from Italy, the head manager of "Metro" Antonio Guglielmi.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian:_FIFA_Ethics_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian:_FIFA_Ethics-41">[41]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:A_New_Dawn_for_Central_Asia_Ivanishvili,_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/A_New_Dawn_for_Central_Asia_Ivanishvili%2C_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg/220px-A_New_Dawn_for_Central_Asia_Ivanishvili%2C_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/A_New_Dawn_for_Central_Asia_Ivanishvili%2C_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg/330px-A_New_Dawn_for_Central_Asia_Ivanishvili%2C_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/A_New_Dawn_for_Central_Asia_Ivanishvili%2C_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg/440px-A_New_Dawn_for_Central_Asia_Ivanishvili%2C_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:A_New_Dawn_for_Central_Asia_Ivanishvili,_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Former 
        <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgian</a> prime minister 
        <a href="/wiki/Bidzina_Ivanishvili" title="Bidzina Ivanishvili">Bidzina Ivanishvili</a> with Azerbaijani president 
        <a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">Ilham Aliyev</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The leak also revealed an extensive <a href="/wiki/Conflict_of_interest" title="Conflict of interest">conflict of interest</a> connection between a member of the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Ethics_Committee" title="FIFA Ethics Committee">FIFA Ethics Committee</a> and former FIFA vice president <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Figueredo" title="Eugenio Figueredo">Eugenio Figueredo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian:_FIFA_Ethics_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian:_FIFA_Ethics-41">[41]</a></sup> Swiss police searched the offices of <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>, European football's governing body, after the naming of former secretary-general <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Infantino" title="Gianni Infantino">Gianni Infantino</a> as president of FIFA. He had signed a television deal while he was at UEFA with a company called Cross Trading, which the FBI has since accused of bribery. The contract emerged among the leaked documents. Infantino has denied wrongdoing.<sup id="cite_ref-uefa_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uefa-43">[43]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Passports of at least 200 Americans were discovered in the Papers, but no US politicians have been named in the leak.<sup id="cite_ref-Power_Players_36-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_Players-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SeattleUS_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SeattleUS-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IBD_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IBD-45">[45]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Mossack Fonseca ran six businesses for Rami Makhlouf, cousin of Syrian president <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a>, despite US sanctions against him.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcSyr_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcSyr-46">[46]</a></sup> DCB Finance, a Virgin Islands-based shell company founded by North Korean banker<sup id="cite_ref-USTreas_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USTreas-47">[47]</a></sup> Kim Chol Sam and British banker <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Cowie" title="Nigel Cowie">Nigel Cowie</a><sup id="cite_ref-Cowie_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cowie-48">[48]</a></sup> also ignored international sanctions and continued to do business with North Korea with the help of the Panamanian firm. The US Department of the Treasury in 2013 called DCB Finance a front company for Daedong Credit Bank and announced sanctions against both companies for providing banking services to Korean arms dealer <a href="/wiki/Korea_Mining_and_Development_Trading_Corporation" title="Korea Mining and Development Trading Corporation">Korea Mining and Development Trading Corporation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-USTreas_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USTreas-47">[47]</a></sup> attempting to evade sanctions against that country, and helping to sell arms and expand <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>'s <a href="/wiki/North_Korea_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="North Korea and weapons of mass destruction">nuclear weapons programme</a>. Cowie said the holding company was used for legitimate business and he was not aware of illicit transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-Cowie_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cowie-48">[48]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to <a href="/wiki/TeleSUR" title="TeleSUR">TeleSUR</a>, United Arab Emirates President <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a> "used the services of Mossack Fonseca to establish at least 30 companies in the British Virgin Islands that owned and operated US$1.7 billion worth of commercial and residential assets for the sheikh in high-end neighborhoods in the United Kingdom."<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Prime Minister of Pakistan <a href="/wiki/Nawaz_Sharif" title="Nawaz Sharif">Nawaz Sharif</a>'s three children  <a href="/wiki/Maryam_Nawaz" title="Maryam Nawaz">Mariam Safdar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sharif_family" title="Sharif family">Hasan and Hussain Nawaz Sharif</a> are among the over 200 members of the Pakistani elite listed in the Panama Papers as owners of offshore companies in a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIRPApr416_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIRPApr416-50">[50]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Popular Indian celebrities such as <a href="/wiki/Amitabh_Bachchan" title="Amitabh Bachchan">Amitabh Bachchan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aishwarya_Rai_Bachchan" title="Aishwarya Rai Bachchan">Aishwarya Rai Bachchan</a> are also involved, along with the real estate developer, DLF owner <a href="/wiki/Kushal_Pal_Singh" title="Kushal Pal Singh">Kushal Pal Singh</a>, and Sameer Gehlaut of the <a href="/wiki/Indiabulls" title="Indiabulls">Indiabulls</a> group, as well as <a href="/wiki/Gautam_Adani" title="Gautam Adani">Gautam Adani</a>'s elder brother Vinod Adani.<sup id="cite_ref-indianexpress1_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indianexpress1-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Indian politicians on the list include <a href="/wiki/Shishir_Bajoria" title="Shishir Bajoria">Shishir Bajoria</a> from West Bengal and <a href="/wiki/Anurag_Kejriwal" title="Anurag Kejriwal">Anurag Kejriwal</a>, the former chief of the Delhi unit of Loksatta Party.<sup id="cite_ref-indianexpress1_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indianexpress1-51">[51]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Actor <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Chan" title="Jackie Chan">Jackie Chan</a> has been mentioned in the leaks as a shareholder of six companies based in the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Among the celebrities involved in this list, the Spanish director <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Almodovar" title="Pedro Almodovar" class="mw-redirect">Pedro Almodovar</a>, who (along with his brother Augustine) created a company called Glen Valley in the British Virgin Islands, which is a tax haven. Mexican actress Edith Gonzalez was related through her husband Lorenzo Lazo, who was a Televisa partner, Veracruz governor, and currently owns an airline online. Similarly, it is ensuring that the president of TV Azteca, Banco Azteca and Azteca Foundation, Benjamin Ricardo Salinas Pliego, used an offshore company set up in the Virgin Islands with Panamanian firm for the purchase of a yacht. Puerto Rican recording artist <a href="/wiki/Daddy_Yankee" title="Daddy Yankee">Daddy Yankee</a> appeared inside the huge leak of information from the Panama Papers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Icelandic_prime_minister">Icelandic prime minister</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Icelandic prime minister">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugssonin_Oct,_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugssonin_Oct%2C_2014.jpg/170px-Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugssonin_Oct%2C_2014.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugssonin_Oct%2C_2014.jpg/255px-Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugssonin_Oct%2C_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugssonin_Oct%2C_2014.jpg/340px-Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugssonin_Oct%2C_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="936" data-file-height="1248"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugssonin_Oct,_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugsson" title="Sigmundur Davíð Gunnlaugsson">Sigmundur Davíð Gunnlaugsson</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Iceland" title="Prime Minister of Iceland">Prime Minister of Iceland</a>, resigned on April 5, 2016
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Anna Sigurlaug Pálsdóttir, the wife of Icelandic prime minister <a href="/wiki/Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugsson" title="Sigmundur Davíð Gunnlaugsson">Sigmundur Davíð Gunnlaugsson</a> held an interest in the country's failed banks through offshore company Wintris Inc. Sigmundur Davíð, elected after the 2008 banking collapse in Iceland, had pledged to clean up corruption in the banking system. The couple bought Wintris in 2007 from Mossack Fonseca through the Luxembourg branch of <a href="/wiki/Landsbanki" title="Landsbanki">Landsbanki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Huffington_Post_Icelandic_PM_2016_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Huffington_Post_Icelandic_PM_2016-54">[54]</a></sup> But Sigmundur Davíð did not declare his interest in the company when he entered parliament in 2009, and did not sell his 50 percent of Wintris to his wifefor US$1until eight months later,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC:_reveal_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_reveal-31">[31]</a></sup> on the day before a new law took effect that would have required him to declare the conflict of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Contacted by ICIJ journalists ahead of publication, the couple issued statements about journalist encroachment on their private lives and insisted on their disclosures were complete and the company paid taxes in Iceland. However, since his position involved negotiating with bank creditors and his wife as a bondholder was among them, citizens felt he had a strong conflict of interest. Calls for a <a href="/wiki/Snap_election" title="Snap election">snap election</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Althing" title="Althing">Althing</a> (the Icelandic Parliament) were expected,<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian:_Iceland_snap_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian:_Iceland_snap-56">[56]</a></sup> but following the papers' release, faced calls for his resignation instead. Between 22,000 and 24,000 people attended an <a href="/wiki/2016_Icelandic_anti-government_protests" title="2016 Icelandic anti-government protests">anti-government protest</a> outside parliament on 4 April 2016, and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a> wondered in a tweet if this constituted the "largest protest by percentage of population in history".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RT_International_Iceland_Protest_2016_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT_International_Iceland_Protest_2016-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McKernan_Iceland_Protest_2016_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKernan_Iceland_Protest_2016-59">[59]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On 4 April 2016, Sigmundur Davíð announced on live television that he would not resign in the wake of the Panama Papers revelations, calling their content "nothing new".<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> He said he had not broken any rules and that his wife did not benefit financially from his decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC:_reveal_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_reveal-31">[31]</a></sup> However, on 5 April, he asked the President of Iceland to dissolve parliament and call for a general election. The president refused, saying it was not clear that other parties supported the move.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Sigmundur Davíð announced his resignation 5 April though later press statements from his office suggested that he merely "stepped aside" for a time.<sup id="cite_ref-Iceland_PM_gone_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iceland_PM_gone-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Iceland_PM_not_quite_gone_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iceland_PM_not_quite_gone-63">[63]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Juan_Armando_Hinojosa">Juan Armando Hinojosa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Juan Armando Hinojosa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>In 2015 <a href="/wiki/Juan_Armando_Hinojosa" title="Juan Armando Hinojosa">Juan Armando Hinojosa Cantú</a>, a close friend of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexican</a> president <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto" title="Enrique Peña Nieto">Enrique Peña Nieto</a>, enlisted Mossack Fonseca to create trusts for accounts worth US$100 million after he was investigated for allegedly giving special favours to the Mexican president and his wife, according to an analysis by ICIJ, who said that the documents showed "a complex offshore network" of nine companies in New Zealand, the United Kingdom, and the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-campri_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campri-64">[64]</a></sup> Described as Peña Nieto's "favorite contractor", Hinojosa's companies have won more than eighty government contracts and received at least US$2.8 billion in state money, The <i>New York Times</i> reported last year.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beneficiaries_of_the_Brink.27s-Mat_robbery">Beneficiaries of the Brink's-Mat robbery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Beneficiaries of the Brink's-Mat robbery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Over £10&nbsp;million of cash from the sale of the gold stolen in the 1983 <a href="/wiki/Brink%27s-Mat_robbery" title="Brink's-Mat robbery">Brink's-Mat robbery</a> was laundered, first unwittingly by and later with the complicity of Mossack Fonseca, through a Panamanian company, Feberion Inc, set up on behalf of an unnamed client twelve months after the robbery. The money was put through Feberion, which had issued <a href="/wiki/Bearer_shares" title="Bearer shares" class="mw-redirect">bearer shares</a> only, and other <a href="/wiki/Front_company" title="Front company" class="mw-redirect">front companies</a>, via banks in Switzerland, Liechtenstein, Jersey, and the Isle of Man. Two nominee directors from <a href="/wiki/Sark" title="Sark">Sark</a> were appointed to Feberion by Jersey-based offshore specialist, Centre Services.<sup id="cite_ref-20160404guardian_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20160404guardian-66">[66]</a></sup> The offshore firms served to recycle the funds through transactions in land and property in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-20160404guardian_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20160404guardian-66">[66]</a></sup> Although the metropolitan police raided the offices of Centre Services in late-1986 in cooperation with the Jersey authorities where they seized papers and the two Feberion bearer shares, it wasn't until 1995 that Brink's-Mat's solicitors were finally able to take control of Feberion and the assets.<sup id="cite_ref-20160404guardian_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20160404guardian-66">[66]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mossack_Fonseca_companies">Mossack Fonseca companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mossack Fonseca companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>Mossack Fonseca has managed more than 300,000 companies over the years,<sup id="cite_ref-to_know_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to_know-12">[12]</a></sup> with the number of active companies peaking at over 80,000 in 2009. Over 210,000 companies in twenty-one jurisdictions figure in the leaks. More than half were incorporated in the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>, others in Panama, the Bahamas, the Seychelles, <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a>, and Samoa. Mossack Fonseca's clients have come from more than 100 countries. Most of the corporate clients were from Hong Kong, Switzerland, the United Kingdom, Luxembourg, Panama, and Cyprus. Mossack Fonseca worked with more than 14,000 banks, law firms, incorporators, and others to set up companies, foundations, and trusts for their clients.<sup id="cite_ref-ICIJ_graphs_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICIJ_graphs-67">[67]</a></sup> Some 3,100 companies listed in the database appear to have ties to US offshore specialists, and 3,500 shareholders of offshore companies list US addresses.<sup id="cite_ref-SeattleUS_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SeattleUS-44">[44]</a></sup> Mossack Fonseca has offices in Nevada and Wyoming.<sup id="cite_ref-KCStar_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KCStar-68">[68]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The leaked documents indicate that about US$2 trillion has passed through the firm's hands.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Several of the holding companies that appear in the documents did business with sanctioned entities, such as arms merchants and relatives of dictators, while the sanctions were in place. The firm provided services to a Seychelles company named Pangates International, which the US government believes supplied aviation fuel to the Syrian government during the current civil war, and continued to handle its paperwork and certify it as a company in good standing, despite sanctions, until August 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcSyr_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcSyr-46">[46]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>More than 500 banks registered nearly 15,600 <a href="/wiki/Shell_company" title="Shell company" class="mw-redirect">shell companies</a> with Mossack Fonseca, with <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a> and its affiliates accounting for more than 2,300 of the total. <a href="/wiki/Dexia" title="Dexia">Dexia</a> and <a href="/wiki/J._Safra_Sarasin" title="J. Safra Sarasin">J. Safra Sarasin</a> of Luxembourg, <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse" title="Credit Suisse">Credit Suisse</a> from the Channel Islands and the Swiss <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS</a> each requested at least 500 offshore companies for their clients.<sup id="cite_ref-ICIJ_graphs_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICIJ_graphs-67">[67]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a> spokesman said, "The allegations are historical, in some cases dating back 20 years, predating our significant, well-publicized reforms implemented over the last few years."<sup id="cite_ref-MyUser_Uk.reuters.com_5_April_2016c_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MyUser_Uk.reuters.com_5_April_2016c-70">[70]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Luxembourg's <a href="/wiki/Nordea" title="Nordea">Nordea</a> Bank requested almost 400 holding companies in <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a> for their customers between 2004 and 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-mordea_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mordea-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yle-nordea_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yle-nordea-72">[72]</a></sup> The Swedish Financial Supervisory Authority (FI) has said that "serious deficiencies" exist in how Nordea monitors for <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a>, and has given the bank two warnings. In 2015 Nordea had to pay the largest possible fineover five million <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">EUR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mordea_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mordea-71">[71]</a></sup> In 2012 Nordea asked <a href="/wiki/Mossack_Fonseca" title="Mossack Fonseca">Mossack Fonseca</a> to change documents retroactively so that three <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Danish</a> customers' power of attorney documents would appear to have been in force since 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-mordea_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mordea-71">[71]</a></sup> The director for Nordea Private Banking, Thorben Sanders, has admitted that before 2009 Nordea did not screen for tax evaders: "In the end of 2009 we decided that our bank shall not be a means of <a href="/wiki/Tax_evasion" title="Tax evasion">tax evasion</a>," said Sanders.<sup id="cite_ref-mordea_71-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mordea-71">[71]</a></sup> Other Swedish banks are also present in the documents, but Nordea occurs 10,902 times and the next most frequently mentioned bank only occurs 764 times.<sup id="cite_ref-SvdVeta3_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SvdVeta3-73">[73]</a></sup> In response to the leaks, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Stefan_L%C3%B6fven" title="Stefan Löfven">Stefan Löfven</a> said he is very critical of Nordea's conduct and role, while Minister of Finance <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_Andersson_(Social_Democrat)" title="Magdalena Andersson (Social Democrat)">Magdalena Andersson</a> characterized the bank's conduct as "totally unacceptable".<sup id="cite_ref-local-nordea_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-local-nordea-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GpSkams_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GpSkams-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mossack_Fonseca_responses">Mossack Fonseca responses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mossack Fonseca responses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>In response to queries from the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Miami_Herald" title="The Miami Herald" class="mw-redirect">The Miami Herald</a></i> and ICIJ, Mossack Fonseca issued a 2,900-word statement. In substance, the response identified legal and compliance regimes around the world that reduce the ability of individuals to use offshore companies for tax avoidance and total anonymity. In particular, they cited the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Action_Task_Force_on_Money_Laundering" title="Financial Action Task Force on Money Laundering">FATF</a> protocols which (for companies and financial institutions in the majority of countries in the world) require identification of ultimate beneficial owners of all companies (including offshore companies) to open accounts and transact business.</p> 
     <p>In an accompanying editor's note, <i>The Miami Herald</i> stated that the Mossack Fonseca statement "did not address any of the specific due diligence failings uncovered by reporters".<sup id="cite_ref-MH_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MH-76">[76]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On Monday, 4 April, Mossack Fonseca released a statement: "Our industry is not particularly well understood by the public, and unfortunately this series of articles will only serve to deepen that confusion. The facts are these: while we may have been the victim of a data breach, nothing we've seen in this illegally obtained cache of documents suggests we've done anything illegal, and that's very much in keeping with the global reputation we've built over the past 40 years of doing business the right way, right here in Panama. Obviously, no one likes to have their property stolen, and we intend to do whatever we can to ensure the guilty parties are brought to justice. But in the meantime, our plan is to continue to serve our clients, stand behind our people, and support the local communities in which we have the privilege to work all over the world, just as we've done for nearly four decades." Firm co-founder <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Fonseca_Mora" title="Ramón Fonseca Mora">Ramón Fonseca Mora</a> told <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> that the information published is false and full of inaccuracies and that parties "in many of the circumstances" cited by the ICIJ "are not and have never been clients of Mossack Fonseca." The firm provided longer statements to ICIJ.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Fonseca also said that the company always have been legal and have been hacked.<sup id="cite_ref-DiePresse.com_2016_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DiePresse.com_2016-78">[78]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In its official statement<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Mossack Fonseca suggested that responsibility for potential legal violations may lie with failures or lapses by other institutions given that:</p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p>approximately 90% of our clientele is comprised of professional clients, such as international financial institutions as well as <a href="/wiki/Trust_company" title="Trust company">trust companies</a> and prominent law and accounting firms, who act as intermediaries and are regulated in the <a href="/wiki/Jurisdiction" title="Jurisdiction">jurisdiction</a> of their business. These clients are obliged to perform <a href="/wiki/Due_diligence" title="Due diligence">due diligence</a> on their clients in accordance with the KYC and AML regulations to which they are subject.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>In an interview <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Mossack" title="Jürgen Mossack">Jürgen Mossack</a> and Ramón Fonseca gave to <i>Bloomberg</i> Mossack said: "The cat's out of the bag, so now we have to deal with the aftermath."<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Ramón Fonseca said the leak was not an "inside job"the company had been hacked by servers based abroad. It filed a complaint with the Panamanian attorney general's office.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On 7 April 2016 is was announced that <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Mossack" title="Jürgen Mossack">Jürgen Mossack</a> was resigning from Panama's Council on Foreign Relations (<a href="/wiki/Consejo_Nacional_de_Relaciones_Exteriores" title="Consejo Nacional de Relaciones Exteriores">Conarex</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Yet, he was not officially serving at the time of his resignation.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> His brother <a href="/wiki/Peter_Mossack" title="Peter Mossack">Peter Mossack</a> still serves as honorary Consul of Panama from 2010 to date.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Responses_in_Panama">Responses in Panama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Responses in Panama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>The Procuraduría de la Nación announced that it will open an investigation concerning the "Panama papers", where Mossack Fonseca is involved.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Minister of the Presidency, Alvaro Alemán categorically rejected that Panama is considered a tax haven and ruled that no permit is used the country as a "scapegoat", thus reacting to the scandal "Panama Papers" and the subsequent re-registration by France in the list of tax havens. Alemán criticized vigorously the statements made by the Secretary General of the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD) José Ángel Gurría and Minister of Finance of France, Michael Sapin and considered as disrespectful and irresponsible, especially when publications speak of a total of 21 jurisdictions, but only lash out at Panama.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Alemán explained that talks have started with the French ambassador in Panama, with whom the issue will be discussed preliminarily and establish avenues of understanding to clarify the situation being implicated the country.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Eduardo Morgan of the Panamanian firm Morgan &amp; Morgan accused the OECD of being behind the campaign to avoid competition that Panama represents for the interests of other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The Panama Papers are a very serious issue for Panama because it affects in an "unfair" manner the country's image and is not the result of an investigation, but is a "hack". This was stated on April 5, by Adolfo Linares, president of the Chamber of Commerce, Industries and Agriculture of Panama (Cciap).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Colegio Nacional de Abogados de Panama (CNA) urged the Panamanian government to sue anyone who has affected the country's image with the massive leak of documents linking the Panamanian firm Mossack Fonseca with the creation of companies to move capital evading taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Political analyst Mario Rognoni said that Panama is the most affected in the whole scandal 'Panama Papers'. He said the world is pointing to Panama as a tax haven and will depend on the policies adopted by the authorities. On the government of President Juan Carlos Varela, he believes he might be involved if he tries to cover up the responsibility of those involved.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Economist Rolando Gordon said this hurts the country that has just emerged from the gray list of FATF. The US could ask Panama to modify the law, he said.</p> 
     <p>He explained that at this time is seen as a scandal, but will each country, especially Panama to conduct investigations and determine whether it is true that illegal or improper acts were committed.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Panama's Lawyers Movement listed as a 'cyber bullying or international cyberterrorism' scandal called 'Panama Papers'. In a press conference, the guild primarily condemned the attack on the country brand 'Panama'. Fraguela Alfonso, president of the movement, said there is no doubt that this is a direct attack on the country's financial system.'I invite all organized forces of the country to create a great crusade for the rescue of the country's image, "he said. He said that Panama is not a tax haven and Panamanian corporations are widely used by the Panamanians. The law firm Rubio, Alvarez, Solis &amp; Abrego also reacted and in a press release detailing that "in recent decades Panama has been in the financial and most important services in Latin America and the world plazas. Product of it all kinds of attacks on our service system 'are encouraged.'<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The establishment of an offshore company is legal. The lawyer and excontralor of the Republic Alvin Weeden explained that illegal is that the product created or sold to others is used for money laundering or arms smuggling, terrorism, tax evasion. This case was published on Twitter: 'Is like you create an atomic bomb, you sell it to another country and detonate them in another country'.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On 12 April, Panamanian prosecutors conducted a raid on Mossack Fonseca, with a search of their Bella Vista offices by the newly formed Second Specialized Prosecutor against Organized Crime, supported by the Panamanian Police. Official sources from the Procuraduría de la Nación confirmed at 4:11 pm, which was a visual inspection as part of the investigation initiated by the international scandal called "The Panama Papers", which links the firm Mossack Fonseca. The Attorney General's office issued a press release following the raid stating that the purpose was "to obtain documents relevant to the information published in news articles that establishes the possible use of the law firm in illegal activities."<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations.2C_reactions.2C_and_investigations">Allegations, reactions, and investigations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Allegations, reactions, and investigations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Reactions_to_the_Panama_Papers" title="Reactions to the Panama Papers">Reactions to the Panama Papers</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Argentina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Presidente_Macri_en_el_Sillon_de_Rivadavia_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Presidente_Macri_en_el_Sillon_de_Rivadavia_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Presidente_Macri_en_el_Sillon_de_Rivadavia_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="170" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Presidente_Macri_en_el_Sillon_de_Rivadavia_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Presidente_Macri_en_el_Sillon_de_Rivadavia_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Presidente_Macri_en_el_Sillon_de_Rivadavia_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Presidente_Macri_en_el_Sillon_de_Rivadavia_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2214" data-file-height="3045"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Presidente_Macri_en_el_Sillon_de_Rivadavia_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Argentine President 
        <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Macri" title="Mauricio Macri">Mauricio Macri</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Argentine president <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Macri" title="Mauricio Macri">Mauricio Macri</a> is listed as head of a trading company based in the Bahamas that he did not disclose during his tenure as <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Government_of_Buenos_Aires" title="Chief of Government of Buenos Aires" class="mw-redirect">Mayor of Buenos Aires</a>; it is not clear whether disclosure of non-equity directorships was then required under Argentine law.<sup id="cite_ref-Fusion:_Wikileaks_of_the_mega-rich_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fusion:_Wikileaks_of_the_mega-rich-37">[37]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On April 7, 2016, federal prosecutor Federico Delgado began a formal investigation into Macri's involvement with Fleg Trading Ltd., the company registered in Panama for which President Macri was listed as director. Judge Sebastián Casanello was asked to start the file on the inquiry.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The initial petition was made by <a href="/wiki/Neuqu%C3%A9n_Province" title="Neuquén Province">Neuquén</a> representative Darío Martínez. Martínez claims Macri could be guilty of perjury due to omissions made in his sworn statement.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Martínez also referenced another offshore company, Kagemusha SA (named after <a href="/wiki/Akira_Kurosawa" title="Akira Kurosawa">Akira Kurosawa's</a> <a href="/wiki/Kagemusha" title="Kagemusha">1980 film</a>), which had been established in 1981 and to which President Macri also had connections.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The family of Argentine football player <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a> announced that they will file a complaint after reports accused him of assembling a tax evasion network in Panama. The family denied Messi had been involved and called the accusations slanderous. They said that the company referred to in the Panama Papers was inactive and that Messi had declared all income from <a href="/wiki/Image_rights" title="Image rights" class="mw-redirect">image rights</a> before and after proceedings with the Argentine Tax Agency.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armenia">Armenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Armenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>On April 4, 2016 <i><a href="/wiki/Hetq_Online" title="Hetq Online">Hetq Online</a></i> reported that according to the Panama Papers, Major-General of Justice and head of the Armenia's <a href="/w/index.php?title=Compulsory_Enforcement_Service&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Compulsory Enforcement Service (page does not exist)">Compulsory Enforcement Service</a> Mihran Poghosyan was connected to three Panama-registered companies (Sigtem Real Estates Inc., Hopkinten Trading Inc. and Bangio Invest S.A., being the sole owner of Sigtem and Hopkinten).<sup id="cite_ref-hetq_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hetq-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> On April 8, Armenian Transparency International Anti-Corruption Center filed a petition with the Ethics Committee for High Level Officials, requesting an investigation of Poghosyan.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Members of the families of Poghosyan's uncles Grigor and Mikhail Haroutyunyan were also mentioned in connection with his business.<sup id="cite_ref-hetq_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hetq-105">[105]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Taxation_Office" title="Australian Taxation Office">Australian Taxation Office</a> has announced that it is investigating 800 individual Australian taxpayers on the Mossack Fonseca list of clients and that some of the cases may be referred to the country's Serious Financial Crime Task Force.<sup id="cite_ref-SMHATOApr416_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMHATOApr416-108">[108]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Azerbaijan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ilham_Aliyev_par_Claude_Truong-Ngoc_juin_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Ilham_Aliyev_par_Claude_Truong-Ngoc_juin_2014.jpg/170px-Ilham_Aliyev_par_Claude_Truong-Ngoc_juin_2014.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Ilham_Aliyev_par_Claude_Truong-Ngoc_juin_2014.jpg/255px-Ilham_Aliyev_par_Claude_Truong-Ngoc_juin_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Ilham_Aliyev_par_Claude_Truong-Ngoc_juin_2014.jpg/340px-Ilham_Aliyev_par_Claude_Truong-Ngoc_juin_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2556" data-file-height="3834"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
