         <a href="/wiki/File:Ilham_Aliyev_par_Claude_Truong-Ngoc_juin_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> President of Azerbaijan 
        <a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">Ilham Aliyev</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijani</a> president <a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">Ilham Aliyev</a> did not respond to repeated requests for comments.<sup id="cite_ref-icij_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icij-109">[109]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to ICIJ website, "The family of Azerbaijan President Ilham Aliyev leads a charmed, glamorous life, thanks in part to financial interests in almost every sector of the economy. ... [Aliyev's daughter] Arzu, has financial stakes in a firm that won rights to mine for gold in the western village of Chovdar and Azerfon, the country's largest mobile phone business. Arzu is also a significant shareholder in SW Holding, which controls nearly every operation related to Azerbaijan Airlines ("Azal"), from meals to airport taxis. Both sisters and brother Heydar own property in Dubai valued at roughly $75 million in 2010; Heydar is the legal owner of nine luxury mansions in Dubai purchased for some $44 million".<sup id="cite_ref-icij_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icij-109">[109]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>According to numerous media outlets, two conglomerates and thirty-two Bangladeshi shareholders are listed. Top business personalities include <a href="/wiki/Aziz_Khan_(businessman)" title="Aziz Khan (businessman)">Muhammed Aziz Khan</a>, Mohiuddin Monem, and <a href="/wiki/Samson_H._Chowdhury" title="Samson H. Chowdhury">Samson H. Chowdhury</a>. Awami League Presidium member <a href="/wiki/Kazi_Zafarullah" title="Kazi Zafarullah">Kazi Zafarullah</a> and his wife <a href="/wiki/Nilufar_Zafar" title="Nilufar Zafar" class="mw-redirect">Nilufar Zafar</a> are said to be in the list.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On April 7, 2016, The <a href="/wiki/Anti_Corruption_Commission_Bangladesh" title="Anti Corruption Commission Bangladesh">Anti Corruption Commission Bangladesh</a> launched an inquiry to obtain details of the businesses and individuals and said that tax evaders would be brought to trial and punished.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Politicians from seven parties in Brazil were named as clients of a Panama-based firm at the center of the massive data leak over possible tax evasion; however, even before the Panama's files were published, in January, 2016, the Brazilian Federal Police, as part of a corruption investigation known as <a href="/wiki/Operation_Car_Wash" title="Operation Car Wash">Operation Car Wash</a>, had already accused Mossack Fonseca's law firm of helping suspects create offshore entities to hide corrupt money. It was alleged by the legal authorities that the firm was using a real estate company in order to help hide money coming from the criminal scheme involving <a href="/wiki/Petrobras" title="Petrobras">Petrobras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The leaked files included politicians from Brazil's largest party, the <a href="/wiki/PMDB" title="PMDB" class="mw-redirect">PMDB</a>, which broke away from President <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a>'s coalition in 2016. Political figures from the <a href="/wiki/PSDB" title="PSDB" class="mw-redirect">PSDB</a>, the most prominent opposition party in the country, was also mentioned in the leaks, as well as others from the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Labour_Party" title="Democratic Labour Party" class="mw-disambig">PDT</a>, PP, PSB, PSD and the PTB parties. No politicians from <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party" title="Workers' Party">Rousseff's party</a> were mentioned in the leaks.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> A research in the Panama Papers, from a group of Dutch journalists from the daily newspaper <i>Trouw</i>, has shown that TV Globo is cited many times in a money laundering investigation of the <a href="/wiki/De_Nederlandsche_Bank" title="De Nederlandsche Bank">De Nederlandsche Bank</a> which revealed that for years the media outlet conducted several irregular financial transactions through tax havens in order to pay broadcast rights for the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Panama Papers also revealed that a former <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court" title="Supreme Federal Court">Supreme Court judge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joaquim_Barbosa" title="Joaquim Barbosa">Barbosa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> bought cash an apartment in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> downtown<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> and that at least 57 people investigated in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Lava_Jato" title="Operation Lava Jato" class="mw-redirect">Operation Lava Jato</a> operated more than 100 offshore companies.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Canadian prime minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Justin Trudeau</a> has denied any involvement with the leak, saying "I have entirely and completely been transparent about mine and my familys finances. That is something I learned early on that Canadians expect from their leaders."<sup id="cite_ref-canada3_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canada3-117">[117]</a></sup> The government has ordered the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Revenue_Agency" title="Canada Revenue Agency">Canada Revenue Agency</a> to find copies of the Panama Papers, in order to find any Canadians that used offshore accounts to avoid taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-canada3_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canada3-117">[117]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Canada" title="Royal Bank of Canada">Royal Bank of Canada</a>'s CEO <a href="/wiki/David_I._McKay" title="David I. McKay">David McKay</a> announced that the bank set up a team that will look back through four decades of documentation for ties to Mossack Fonseca.<sup id="cite_ref-canada1_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canada1-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-canada2_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canada2-119">[119]</a></sup> CEO <a href="/wiki/Bill_Downe" title="Bill Downe">Bill Downe</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Montreal" title="Bank of Montreal">Bank of Montreal</a> also defended, saying "Canadian banks have 'dramatically' beefed up anti-money laundering controls over the last seven to 10 years." He also stated that any link between Canadian businesses and the Panama Papers would have originated a long time ago, before the time when Canadian banks took action to stop money laundering.<sup id="cite_ref-canada1_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canada1-118">[118]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Xi_Jinping_October_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Xi_Jinping_October_2015.jpg/170px-Xi_Jinping_October_2015.jpg" width="170" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Xi_Jinping_October_2015.jpg/255px-Xi_Jinping_October_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Xi_Jinping_October_2015.jpg/340px-Xi_Jinping_October_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="1163"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Xi_Jinping_October_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="President of the People's Republic of China">Chinese president</a> 
        <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Relatives of highly placed Chinese officials including seven senior leaders and former senior leaders of <a href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Politburo of the Communist Party of China">Politburo of the Communist Party of China</a> have been named, including former Premier <a href="/wiki/Li_Peng" title="Li Peng">Li Peng</a>'s daughter <a href="/wiki/Li_Xiaolin" title="Li Xiaolin">Li Xiaolin</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party</a> General Secretary <a href="/wiki/Hu_Yaobang" title="Hu Yaobang">Hu Yaobang</a>'s son <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hu_Dehua&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hu Dehua (page does not exist)">Hu Dehua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deng_Jiagui" title="Deng Jiagui">Deng Jiagui</a>, the brother-in-law of current <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of China">General Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a>. Deng had two shell companies in the British Virgin Islands while Xi was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Politburo_Standing_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Politburo Standing Committee of the Communist Party of China">Politburo Standing Committee</a>, but they were dormant by the time Xi became General Secretary of Communist Party (<a href="/wiki/Paramount_leader" title="Paramount leader">paramount leader</a>) in 2012. Others named include the son and daughter-in-law of propaganda chief <a href="/wiki/Liu_Yunshan" title="Liu Yunshan">Liu Yunshan</a> and the son-in-law of Vice-Premier <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Gaoli" title="Zhang Gaoli">Zhang Gaoli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MP_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MP-120">[120]</a></sup> China's government <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_China" title="Internet censorship in China">is suppressing</a> mentions of the Panama Papers on social media and in search engines results.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> China's Communist Party reportedly has told news organizations to delete all content related to the Panama Papers leak.</p> 
     <p>Considering the material to be a concerted foreign media attack on China, internet information offices were immediately given verbal orders to delete reprinted reports on the Panama Papers, and not to follow up on related content without exceptions. <a href="/wiki/Hong_Lei_(diplomat)" title="Hong Lei (diplomat)">Hong Lei</a>, the spokesman of China's foreign ministry, responded that he had "no comment" for "such groundless accusations" at an April 5 news conference.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Chinese authorities have <a href="/wiki/Censorship_in_China" title="Censorship in China">blocked almost all information</a> about the Panama Papers on Chinese media and the Internet. A screenshot showed that the authority had forced all websites to delete content about the Panama Papers.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Foreign websites such as <a href="/wiki/Wikileak" title="Wikileak" class="mw-redirect">Wikileak</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Digital_Times" title="China Digital Times">China Digital Times</a> have been <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Firewall" title="The Great Firewall" class="mw-redirect">blocked</a> in mainland China. On <a href="/wiki/Sina_Weibo" title="Sina Weibo">Sina Weibo</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">twitter</a>-like social media in China, almost all content about the Panama Papers was deleted. Because Xi's brother-in-law had been named, and the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a> is well known, Weibo users started to use "brother-in-law", "Canal Papers", and other such tags to avoid Weibo's censor.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Despite the censorship, Weibo search ranking was topped by phrases "seemingly related" to the Panama Papers since its global press coverage such as "tax evasion", "document", "leak" and "Putin".<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">Colombia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Colombia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Directorate_of_Taxes_and_Customs" title="National Directorate of Taxes and Customs">National Directorate of Taxes and Customs</a> launched an investigation into all 850 clients of Mossack Fonseca Colombia, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Mossack_Fonseca" title="Mossack Fonseca">Mossack Fonseca</a> that was established in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> In 2014, Colombia had placed Panama onto its blacklist of tax havens.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The leaked documents also lead Panama to move forward on the ongoing negotiations with Colombia on tax information-sharing.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cyprus">Cyprus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cyprus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Cyprus" title="Central Bank of Cyprus">Central Bank of Cyprus</a> officially declared: "With regard to press reports citing leaked documents, known as the Panama Papers, the Central Bank of Cyprus announces that it is assessing the information to the extent that it may concern the Cypriot banking system and taking, where necessary, appropriate action."<sup id="cite_ref-CM_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CM-129">[129]</a></sup> A Cypriot online paper said "The Cyprus link stems from the fact that Fonseca runs an office in Cyprus and, more specifically, in <a href="/wiki/Limassol" title="Limassol">Limassol</a>. In a chart, the leaks name Cyprus as a tax haven (countries that offer little or no tax), although it has a corporate tax rate of 12.5%, the same as Ireland."<sup id="cite_ref-CM_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CM-129">[129]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Many senior EU figures have been implicated in the Panama Papers scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-Politico_EU_figures_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Politico_EU_figures-130">[130]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Taxation_and_Customs_Union,_Audit_and_Anti-Fraud" title="European Commissioner for Taxation and Customs Union, Audit and Anti-Fraud">European Commissioner for Taxation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Moscovici" title="Pierre Moscovici">Pierre Moscovici</a>, has said that the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> as a whole had a "duty" to prevent the kind of tax avoidance uncovered in the Panama Papers scandal. Moscovici told reporters the use of offshore companies to hide what he called "shocking amounts" of financial assets from tax authorities was "unethical". He estimated that the tax shelters resulted in an annual loss of some 1 trillion in public finances, adding that the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> attempted to tighten tax rules across the union since November 2014 due to the <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Leaks" title="Luxembourg Leaks">"LuxLeaks"</a> tax avoidance scandal (also revealed by the ICIJ), and hoped the extent of the Panama Papers revelations would spur countries to action.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In a 2013 letter unearthed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> to the then president of the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herman_Van_Rompuy" title="Herman Van Rompuy">Herman Van Rompuy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> said that offshore trusts should not automatically be subject to the same transparency requirements as shell companies.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Some analysts suggest that these actions may have an impact on the outcome of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">the upcoming referendum</a> on UK membership of the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hosni_Mubarak_ritratto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Hosni_Mubarak_ritratto.jpg/170px-Hosni_Mubarak_ritratto.jpg" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Hosni_Mubarak_ritratto.jpg/255px-Hosni_Mubarak_ritratto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Hosni_Mubarak_ritratto.jpg/340px-Hosni_Mubarak_ritratto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hosni_Mubarak_ritratto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Former Egyptian President 
        <a href="/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak" title="Hosni Mubarak">Hosni Mubarak</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Alaa_Mubarak" title="Alaa Mubarak">Alaa Mubarak</a>, son of former president <a href="/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak" title="Hosni Mubarak">Hosni Mubarak</a>, was cited as owning, through holding companies, real estate properties in London.<sup id="cite_ref-campri_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campri-64">[64]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>French financial prosecutors opened a probe, and President <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="François Hollande">François Hollande</a> declared that tax evaders would be brought to trial and punished.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Also as a result, France restored Panama to its tax havens list, from which it had recently been removed.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_Le_Pen" title="Jean-Marie Le Pen">Jean-Marie Le Pen</a>, founder and long-time leader of the far-right-wing <a href="/wiki/Front_National" title="Front National" class="mw-redirect">Front National</a> is mentioned in the documents, along with several aides of his daughter <a href="/wiki/Marine_Le_Pen" title="Marine Le Pen">Marine Le Pen</a>, the current party leader.<sup id="cite_ref-campri_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campri-64">[64]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iceland">Iceland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Iceland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>On April 5, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Iceland" title="Prime Minister of Iceland">Prime Minister of Iceland</a> <a href="/wiki/Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugsson" title="Sigmundur Davíð Gunnlaugsson">Sigmundur Davíð Gunnlaugsson</a> announced his resignation.<sup id="cite_ref-Iceland_PM_gone_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iceland_PM_gone-62">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk_City_Council" title="Reykjavík City Council">Reykjavík City Council</a> Member <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAl%C3%ADus_V%C3%ADfill_Ingvarsson" title="Júlíus Vífill Ingvarsson">Júlíus Vífill Ingvarsson</a> resigned earlier in the day.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Shortly after initial reports of Sigmundur Davíð's resignation, the Prime Minister's office in Iceland issued a statement to the international press saying that Sigmundur Davíð has not resigned, but rather stepped aside for an unspecified amount of time and will continue to serve as the Chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Party_(Iceland)" title="Progressive Party (Iceland)">Progressive Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Iceland_PM_not_quite_gone_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iceland_PM_not_quite_gone-63">[63]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_India" title="Prime Minister of India">Indian prime minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a> ordered an inquiry, and subsequently the Indian government announced that it was constituting a special multi-agency group comprising officers from the investigative unit of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Board_of_Direct_Taxes" title="Central Board of Direct Taxes" class="mw-redirect">Central Board of Direct Taxes</a> and its Foreign Tax and Tax Research Division, the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Intelligence_Unit" title="Financial Intelligence Unit" class="mw-redirect">Financial Intelligence Unit</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_India" title="Reserve Bank of India">Reserve Bank of India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Finance Minister, Bambang P.S. Brodjonegoro, immediately responded quickly to the leaked data of tax evasion "Panama Papers" by instructing the directorate general of taxation (DGT) to follow up the findings. Leaked investment data originating from Panama law firm, Mossack Fonseca, attracted Bambang's attention because they can be a source of new information about the potential tax that has not been traced.</p> 
     <p>"I've asked Mr Ken (Dwijugiasteadi), Director General of Taxation, please let's study the data known as Panama Papers", he said at the headquarters of the DGT, Tuesday (5/4).</p> 
     <p>The finance minister once said there is potential for the property of the taxpayer around Rp 4,000 trillion, which has not been affected by the tax. He specifies, around Rp 1,400 trillion, is a property that is not taxed, and remitted to the DGT, while the remaining Rp 2,700 trillion, a rich Indonesian deposits in banks abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Some 600 Israeli companies and 850 Israeli shareholders are listed. Among the Israeli names found in the leaked documents are: top attorney <a href="/wiki/Dov_Weissglass" title="Dov Weissglass">Dov Weissglass</a>, who was the bureau chief of deceased prime minister <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Sharon" title="Ariel Sharon">Ariel Sharon</a>; <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Engel" title="Jacob Engel">Jacob Engel</a>, a businessman active in the African mining industry; and <a href="/wiki/Idan_Ofer" title="Idan Ofer">Idan Ofer</a>, a member of one of Israel's wealthiest families, according to Haaretz.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Tareq Abbas, a son of <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a>, the president of the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority" class="mw-redirect">Palestinian Authority</a>, was also revealed to hold $1 million in shares of an offshore company associated with the Palestinian Authority.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Weissglass' name appears as a sole owner of one of four companies set up by his business partner Assaf Halkin. The company, Talaville Global, was registered in the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a> in May 2012, according to Haaretz, and seven months later, all of its shares were mortgaged against a loan from a <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> bank.</p> 
     <p>Weissglass and Halkin told Haaretz that the company "was registered for the purpose of receiving a loan from the bank in order to invest in European properties. The bank would only allow a loan to a corporation... [the] company activity is reported to the tax authorities in Israel. The required tax on the said activity is paid in Israel."<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Silvio_Berlusconi_in_2015.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Silvio_Berlusconi_in_2015.jpeg/170px-Silvio_Berlusconi_in_2015.jpeg" width="170" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Silvio_Berlusconi_in_2015.jpeg/255px-Silvio_Berlusconi_in_2015.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Silvio_Berlusconi_in_2015.jpeg/340px-Silvio_Berlusconi_in_2015.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="589" data-file-height="810"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Silvio_Berlusconi_in_2015.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi" title="Silvio Berlusconi">Silvio Berlusconi</a>, former Prime Minister of Italy
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>On April 6, 2016 Italy's Procura of Turin ordered <a href="/wiki/Guardia_di_Finanza" title="Guardia di Finanza">Guardia di Finanza</a> further investigation regarding the 800 Italians contained in the Panama Paper's documents.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Former long-time Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi" title="Silvio Berlusconi">Silvio Berlusconi</a>, who had been already convicted for tax evasion and expelled from the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Parliament" title="Italian Parliament">Parliament</a>, was cited on the list.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Other notable people who had been cited on the papers were entrepreneurs <a href="/wiki/Luca_Cordero_di_Montezemolo" title="Luca Cordero di Montezemolo">Luca Cordero di Montezemolo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flavio_Briatore" title="Flavio Briatore">Flavio Briatore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adriano_Galliani" title="Adriano Galliani">Adriano Galliani</a> and actor <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Verdone" title="Carlo Verdone">Carlo Verdone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malta">Malta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Malta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Konrad_Mizzi" title="Konrad Mizzi">Konrad Mizzi</a>, the Minister for Energy and Water Conservation has been identified as being included in the Panama Papers related to a secretive company in Panama through <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> with encouragement of investments by banks.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alliednewspapersltd_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alliednewspapersltd-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alliednewspapersltd_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alliednewspapersltd-151">[151]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:14-02-2013_VISITA_DE_EPN_A_BAH%C3%8DA_DE_BANDERAS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/14-02-2013_VISITA_DE_EPN_A_BAH%C3%8DA_DE_BANDERAS.jpg/170px-14-02-2013_VISITA_DE_EPN_A_BAH%C3%8DA_DE_BANDERAS.jpg" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/14-02-2013_VISITA_DE_EPN_A_BAH%C3%8DA_DE_BANDERAS.jpg/255px-14-02-2013_VISITA_DE_EPN_A_BAH%C3%8DA_DE_BANDERAS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/14-02-2013_VISITA_DE_EPN_A_BAH%C3%8DA_DE_BANDERAS.jpg/340px-14-02-2013_VISITA_DE_EPN_A_BAH%C3%8DA_DE_BANDERAS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="564" data-file-height="761"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:14-02-2013_VISITA_DE_EPN_A_BAH%C3%8DA_DE_BANDERAS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The leaked files identified the "favourite contractor" of Mexican President 
        <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto" title="Enrique Peña Nieto">Enrique Peña Nieto</a>
        <sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Aristóteles Núñez, who is in charge of the government's tax administration, <a href="//es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Servicio_de_Administraci%C3%B3n_Tributaria" class="extiw" title="es:Servicio de Administración Tributaria">Servicio de Administración Tributaria</a>, said that people involved in the Panama Papers case can still make tax declarations and pay taxes on their investments. Being Mexican and having foreign investments or bank accounts is not a crime, but having income and not declaring it is illegal. If the concealment of income from Panama Papers-related investments is categorized as tax evasion, fines of up to 100% of the omitted tax payment can result, as well as three months to nine years imprisonment for a "tax crime".<sup id="cite_ref-AristApr416_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AristApr416-153">[153]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to <i>Forbes</i>, "<a href="/wiki/Hinojosa" title="Hinojosa" class="mw-disambig">Hinojosa</a> and other prominent Mexicans, mostly businessmen with close ties to the government, including at least one member of the Forbes billionaires list, were the subject of extensive articles published on line by <i><a href="/wiki/Proceso_(magazine)" title="Proceso (magazine)">Proceso</a></i> and <i>Aristegui Noticias Sunday</i> to coincide with the ICIJ posting of the Panama Papers."<sup id="cite_ref-fobers_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fobers-154">[154]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>New Zealand's <a href="/wiki/Inland_Revenue_Department_(New_Zealand)" title="Inland Revenue Department (New Zealand)">Inland Revenue Department</a> said that they were working to obtain details of people who have <a href="/wiki/Tax_residence" title="Tax residence">tax residence</a> in the country who may have been involved in arrangements facilitated by Mossack Fonseca.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Gerard_Ryle" title="Gerard Ryle">Gerard Ryle</a>, director of the <a href="/wiki/International_Consortium_of_Investigative_Journalists" title="International Consortium of Investigative Journalists">International Consortium of Investigative Journalists</a>, told Radio New Zealand on 8 April 2016 that New Zealand is a well-known tax haven and a "nice front for criminals".<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norway">Norway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Norway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Tax_Administration" title="Norwegian Tax Administration">Norwegian Tax Administration</a> expects to demand access to information from <a href="/wiki/DNB_ASA" title="DNB ASA">DNB</a> (Norway's largest financial services group) about approximately 30 companies formed by DNB that are owned by Norwegians, 20 of whom are living in Norway.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> 200 Norwegians are on the client list of Mossack Fonseca.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Nawaz_Sharif_January_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Nawaz_Sharif_January_2015.jpg/170px-Nawaz_Sharif_January_2015.jpg" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Nawaz_Sharif_January_2015.jpg/255px-Nawaz_Sharif_January_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Nawaz_Sharif_January_2015.jpg/340px-Nawaz_Sharif_January_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="532" data-file-height="727"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Nawaz_Sharif_January_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Nawaz_Sharif" title="Nawaz Sharif">Nawaz Sharif</a>&nbsp; Prime Minister of 
        <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The three children of Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Nawaz_Sharif" title="Nawaz Sharif">Nawaz Sharif</a>, Maryam, Hussein and Hassan, are shown as owning four companies among them.<sup id="cite_ref-pk_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pk-159">[159]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maryam_Nawaz" title="Maryam Nawaz">Maryam Nawaz</a> denied all such charges via her official <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> account in a series of tweets, saying:<sup id="cite_ref-SamaaApr416_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SamaaApr416-160">[160]</a></sup></p> 
     <blockquote class="templatequote"> 
      <p>As stated earlier, I do not own any company/property abroad. My brother has made me a trustee in one of his corporations which only entitles me to distribute assets to my brother Hussain's family/children if needed. Nothing more than what my brother has already explained. The info provided by leaks does not say any wrongdoing involved. Distortion is wilful that a couple of media channels using to settle scores.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>Samina Durrani, the mother-in-law of chief minister <a href="/wiki/Shebaz_Sharif" title="Shebaz Sharif" class="mw-redirect">Shebaz Sharif</a> from his second marriage and Ilyas Mehraj, his brother-in-law from his first marriage are also included in the documents.The late <a href="/wiki/Benazir_Bhutto" title="Benazir Bhutto">Benazir Bhutto</a> and her nephew are also mentioned.<sup id="cite_ref-pk_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pk-159">[159]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Arkady_Rotenberg.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Vladimir_Putin_and_Arkady_Rotenberg.jpeg/240px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Arkady_Rotenberg.jpeg" width="240" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Vladimir_Putin_and_Arkady_Rotenberg.jpeg/360px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Arkady_Rotenberg.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Vladimir_Putin_and_Arkady_Rotenberg.jpeg/480px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Arkady_Rotenberg.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="678"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Arkady_Rotenberg.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Russian president 
        <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> with Russian businessman and oligarch 
        <a href="/wiki/Arkady_Rotenberg" title="Arkady Rotenberg">Arkady Rotenberg</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCddeutsche_Zeitung" title="Süddeutsche Zeitung">Süddeutsche Zeitung</a></i>, which made the papers public, has described the connections of various individuals listed in the papers to Russian president <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>. According to the newspaper, the release of the papers confirms the previous descriptions of Russia as a <a href="/wiki/Kleptocracy" title="Kleptocracy">kleptocratic</a> "Mafia state" run by Putin and his inner circle.<sup id="cite_ref-sd_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sd-161">[161]</a></sup> Vladimir Putin does not appear in any of the records but the names of many of his associates do, such as construction billionaires <a href="/wiki/Arkady_Rotenberg" title="Arkady Rotenberg">Arkady</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boris_Romanovich_Rotenberg" title="Boris Romanovich Rotenberg">Boris Rotenberg</a>, as well as the professional musician <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Roldugin" title="Sergei Roldugin">Sergei Roldugin</a> and business magnate <a href="/wiki/Alisher_Usmanov" title="Alisher Usmanov">Alisher Usmanov</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Putin_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Putin-162">[162]</a></sup> The papers also list billionaire <a href="/wiki/Gennady_Timchenko" title="Gennady Timchenko">Gennady Timchenko</a>, Putin's press secretary's spouse, his cousin, Putin's former <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a> colleagues, and several oligarchs as owning offshore shell companies. In 2011 Putin had criticized offshore companies as "unpatriotic".<sup id="cite_ref-sd_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sd-161">[161]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The documents leaked indicated that <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Roldugin" title="Sergei Roldugin">Sergei Roldugin</a>, a professional <a href="/wiki/Cello" title="Cello">cellist</a> described by <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Gazeta" title="Novaya Gazeta">Novaya Gazeta</a> as <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>'s best friend and the godfather of his eldest daughter, had acquired assets worth at least $100 million, including a 12.5% stake in Video International, Russia's largest television advertising firm.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Putin_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Putin-162">[162]</a></sup> It was also revealed that Roldugin had acquired these assets in what the <i><a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a></i> described as "suspicious deals".<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_2016_ppp_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_2016_ppp-163">[163]</a></sup> Asked by journalists of Novaya Gazeta about his offshore accounts<sup id="cite_ref-NG_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NG-164">[164]</a></sup> Rodulgin said "I have to take a look and find out what I can say and what I can't", because, he said, financial matters are "delicate".<sup id="cite_ref-NG_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NG-164">[164]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Putin spokesperson <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Peskov" title="Dmitry Peskov">Dmitry Peskov</a> said that Western mainstream media reporting of the Panama Papers was engaged in "Putinophobia". He said the primary target of the leak was <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> and the Panama Papers were part of a conspiracy against Russia, orchestrated by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">United States Department of State</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-Putinphobia2_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Putinphobia2-165">[165]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>President Putin has denied "any element of corruption" over the Panama Papers leaks, saying his opponents are trying to destabilise Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Salman_bin_Abdull_aziz_December_9,_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Salman_bin_Abdull_aziz_December_9%2C_2013.jpg/220px-Salman_bin_Abdull_aziz_December_9%2C_2013.jpg" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Salman_bin_Abdull_aziz_December_9%2C_2013.jpg/330px-Salman_bin_Abdull_aziz_December_9%2C_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Salman_bin_Abdull_aziz_December_9%2C_2013.jpg/440px-Salman_bin_Abdull_aziz_December_9%2C_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1360" data-file-height="1386"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Salman_bin_Abdull_aziz_December_9,_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> King 
        <a href="/wiki/Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Salman of Saudi Arabia">Salman of Saudi Arabia</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Initially, aside from few independent outlets, Russian media entirely ignored the leak. <i>Channel 1</i> and <i>Rossiya 1</i>, both state owned, did not mention the Panama Papers at all on April 4, when the story broke. When an opposition politician asked why the media was ignoring the story, <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Konstantinovich_Kiselyov" title="Dmitry Konstantinovich Kiselyov">Dmitry Kiselev</a>, head of <i><a href="/wiki/Rossiya_Segodnya" title="Rossiya Segodnya">Rossiya Segodnya</a></i>, refused to discuss or comment.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> To the extent that some coverage was given to the story it was often done in the middle of the night, and focused exclusively on international celebrities rather than the links to Putin's circles found in the papers.<sup id="cite_ref-atl_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atl-168">[168]</a></sup> Coverage of the leak began to appear after Peskov's reaction, but generally focused on Peskov's comments rather than discussing the information in the Panama Papers.<sup id="cite_ref-atl_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atl-168">[168]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saudi_Arabia">Saudi Arabia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Saudi Arabia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Salman of Saudi Arabia">King Salman</a> has been mentioned in the leaks in relation to two British Virgin Islands companies taking mortgages in excess of US$34 million to purchase property in central London. His role has not been specified.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Crown Prince <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_bin_Nayef" title="Muhammad bin Nayef">Muhammad bin Nayef</a> has also been named in association with the papers.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_(Singapore)" title="Ministry of Finance (Singapore)">Ministry of Finance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monetary_Authority_of_Singapore" title="Monetary Authority of Singapore">Monetary Authority of Singapore</a> said in a statement that "Singapore takes a serious view on tax evasion and will not tolerate its business and financial centre being used to facilitate tax related crimes. If there is evidence of wrongdoing by any individual or entity in Singapore, we will not hesitate to take firm action."<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Soria_2015b_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Soria_2015b_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Soria_2015b_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="170" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Soria_2015b_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Soria_2015b_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Soria_2015b_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Soria_2015b_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="508" data-file-height="728"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Soria_2015b_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Soria" title="José Manuel Soria">José Manuel Soria</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Industry_(Spain)" title="Ministry of Industry (Spain)">Minister of Industry of Spain</a>, resigned on 
        <a href="/wiki/April_15" title="April 15">April 15</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/2016" title="2016">2016</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>On 15 April 2016, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Soria" title="José Manuel Soria">José Manuel Soria</a> was forced to renounce his post as acting <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Industry_(Spain)" title="Ministry of Industry (Spain)">Minister of Industry, Energy and Tourism</a> because of his involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Panama_papers" title="Panama papers" class="mw-redirect">Panama papers</a> scandal, owing to the leaking of information revealing that he and his family had maintained several <a href="/wiki/Offshore_company" title="Offshore company">offshore societies</a> on <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax havens</a> during the previous decades.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Soria initially claimed the falsehood of such claims, but during the ensuing days proof kept leaking that contradicted his initial version. On 14 April, after it was revealed that he had owned one of such societies on <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> until 2002 during his term as Mayor of <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas" title="Las Palmas">Las Palmas</a>, he was put in a critical political position as a result of his confusing and changing explanations on the issue, resulting in his renounce the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Spain's Soria became the second big casualty of the Panama Papers following Iceland's <a href="/wiki/Sigmundur_Dav%C3%AD%C3%B0_Gunnlaugsson" title="Sigmundur Davíð Gunnlaugsson">Sigmundur Davíð Gunnlaugsson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The Swedish <a href="/wiki/Financial_Supervisory_Authority_(Sweden)" title="Financial Supervisory Authority (Sweden)">Financial Supervisory Authority</a> (FI) said on April 4, 2016 it would launch an investigation into the actions of <a href="/wiki/Nordea" title="Nordea">Nordea</a>, one of the largest financial institutions in the Nordic countries, after Panama Papers revealed the company's Luxembourg office had helped to set up nearly 400 offshore companies for its clients. Later FI said that they would also investigate the other three big banks in Sweden: Handelsbanken, SEB and Swedbank. Nordea cut all ties with Mossack Fonseca following an interview with Nordea CEO <a href="/wiki/Casper_von_Koskull" title="Casper von Koskull">Casper von Koskull</a> on <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Television" title="Sveriges Television">SVT</a> on April 4.<sup id="cite_ref-local-nordea_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-local-nordea-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yle-nordea_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yle-nordea-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> The FI has pointed out that there are "serious deficiencies" in how Nordea monitors <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> and has given the bank two warnings. In 2015 Nordea had to pay the largest possible fine&nbsp; over 5 million <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">EUR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mordea_71-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mordea-71">[71]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Bangkok_Post" title="Bangkok Post">Bangkok Post</a></i> said that the "...<a href="/wiki/Anti-Money_Laundering_Office" title="Anti-Money Laundering Office" class="mw-redirect">Anti-Money Laundering Office</a> (AMLO) is seeking information from its foreign counterparts regarding twenty-one Thai nationals reportedly included in a list of people worldwide using a Panama-based law firm apparently specializing in money laundering and tax evasion. It is not clear why AMLO is investigating only twenty-one. The Panama Papers include at least 780 names of individuals based in Thailand and another fifty companies based in Thailand. Some are foreigners or foreign-owned companies, but 634 individual addresses in Thailand appear in the documents that have surfaced to date, including the CEOs of giant companies <a href="/wiki/Bangkok_Land" title="Bangkok Land">Bangkok Land</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Phatra_Finance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Phatra Finance (page does not exist)">Phatra Finance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tunisia">Tunisia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Tunisia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The Tunis trial court prosecutor ordered a judicial inquiry opened into the Panama Papers and the Tunisian political figures suspected of hiring the firm. A judge from the Financial Judiciary Pole that is a Tunisian specialized court in financial crimes was assigned to the case.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisian</a> <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_Representatives_of_the_People" title="Assembly of the Representatives of the People">Assembly of the Representatives of the People</a> established a parliamentary commission of inquiry as well<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Petro_Porochenko_au_Conseil_de_l%E2%80%99Europe_Strasbourg_26_juin_2014_04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Petro_Porochenko_au_Conseil_de_l%E2%80%99Europe_Strasbourg_26_juin_2014_04.jpg/170px-Petro_Porochenko_au_Conseil_de_l%E2%80%99Europe_Strasbourg_26_juin_2014_04.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Petro_Porochenko_au_Conseil_de_l%E2%80%99Europe_Strasbourg_26_juin_2014_04.jpg/255px-Petro_Porochenko_au_Conseil_de_l%E2%80%99Europe_Strasbourg_26_juin_2014_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Petro_Porochenko_au_Conseil_de_l%E2%80%99Europe_Strasbourg_26_juin_2014_04.jpg/340px-Petro_Porochenko_au_Conseil_de_l%E2%80%99Europe_Strasbourg_26_juin_2014_04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2689" data-file-height="4033"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Petro_Porochenko_au_Conseil_de_l%E2%80%99Europe_Strasbourg_26_juin_2014_04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Ukrainian president 
        <a href="/wiki/Petro_Poroshenko" title="Petro Poroshenko">Petro Poroshenko</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>When Ukrainian president <a href="/wiki/Petro_Poroshenko" title="Petro Poroshenko">Petro Poroshenko</a> ran for office in 2014, he pledged to sell his candy business (<a href="/wiki/Roshen" title="Roshen">Roshen</a>) if elected, but leaked documents indicate that on August 21, 2014 he instead had Mossack Fonseca set up offshore holding company Prime Asset Partners Ltd in the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a> and moved his company there, roughly two months after the election.The move had the potential to save him millions of dollars on his Ukrainian taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-Poroshenko_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poroshenko-179">[179]</a></sup> Records in Cyprus show him as the firm's only shareholder.<sup id="cite_ref-Poroshenko2_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poroshenko2-180">[180]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Anti-corruption group <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a> believes that the "creation of businesses while serving as president is a direct violation of the constitution".<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_2016_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_2016-181">[181]</a></sup> Also, journalists from the <a href="/wiki/Organized_Crime_and_Corruption_Reporting_Project" title="Organized Crime and Corruption Reporting Project">Organized Crime and Corruption Reporting Project</a> believe that with the move Poroshenko committed two other illegalities, starting a new business while in office and failing afterwards to report it on his disclosure statements.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_2016_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_2016-181">[181]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Poroshenko denied any wrongdoing and a spokesman said the offshore company had no active assets and was a legitimate corporate restructure aimed at helping to sell Poroshenko's <a href="/wiki/Roshen" title="Roshen">Roshen group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_2016_181-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_2016-181">[181]</a></sup> Analysts in Ukraine responded that the secretive way Poroshenko set up these accounts was certain to undermine trust in him, <a href="/wiki/Petro_Poroshenko_Bloc" title="Petro Poroshenko Bloc" class="mw-redirect">his party</a> and Ukraine itself.<sup id="cite_ref-KyivPost_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KyivPost-182">[182]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The news about Poroshenko's offshore business came as his government campaigned against offshore companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Poroshenko_179-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poroshenko-179">[179]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oleh_Lyashko" title="Oleh Lyashko">Oleh Lyashko</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Radical_Party_of_Oleh_Lyashko" title="Radical Party of Oleh Lyashko">Radical Party</a>, urged lawmakers to begin impeachment proceedings,<sup id="cite_ref-Poroshenko_179-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poroshenko-179">[179]</a></sup> And even some of his allies backed calls for a parliamentary commission to investigate the allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-Poroshenko_179-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poroshenko-179">[179]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Parliament" title="Ukrainian Parliament" class="mw-redirect">Ukrainian Parliament</a>, relations between the <a href="/wiki/Petro_Poroshenko_Bloc_%22Solidarity%22" title="Petro Poroshenko Bloc &quot;Solidarity&quot;">Poroshenko bloc</a> and the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Front_(Ukraine)" title="People's Front (Ukraine)">People's Front party</a> of Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Arseniy_Yatsenyuk" title="Arseniy Yatsenyuk">Arseniy Yatsenyuk</a> had over previous months already soured, with mutual accusations of <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Ukraine" title="Corruption in Ukraine">corruption</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Poroshenko_179-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poroshenko-179">[179]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Arab_Emirates">United Arab Emirates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: United Arab Emirates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>ICIJ, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> have reported that <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">UAE</a> President <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a> owns London real estate worth more than £1.2 billion through a structure of some thirty shell companies Mossack Fonseca set up for him in the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a> and administer for him, using them to manage and control the luxury properties in London.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guae_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guae-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12_world_leaders_linked_to_offshore_dealings_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12_world_leaders_linked_to_offshore_dealings-185">[185]</a></sup> By December 2015, Mossack Fonseca held nearly all of the shares in those companies in trust structures on his behalf, with the President and his wife, son and daughter the trust beneficiaries.<sup id="cite_ref-12_world_leaders_linked_to_offshore_dealings_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12_world_leaders_linked_to_offshore_dealings-185">[185]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" width="40" height="22" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="759" data-file-height="415"></td> 
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a href="//en.wikinews.org/wiki/Thousands_march_in_London_calling_for_David_Cameron%27s_resignation_over_tax_affairs" class="extiw" title="wikinews:Thousands march in London calling for David Cameron's resignation over tax affairs">Thousands march in London calling for David Cameron's resignation over tax affairs</a></b></i></td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, "More than £170bn of UK property is now held overseas. ... Nearly one in 10 of the 31,000 tax haven companies that own British property are linked to Mossack Fonseca."<sup id="cite_ref-auto_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-real_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-real-186">[186]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:David_Cameron_official.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/David_Cameron_official.jpg/170px-David_Cameron_official.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/David_Cameron_official.jpg/255px-David_Cameron_official.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/David_Cameron_official.jpg/340px-David_Cameron_official.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1412" data-file-height="1887"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:David_Cameron_official.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(United_Kingdom)" title="Leader of the Opposition (United Kingdom)">Leader of the Opposition</a> has called for an immediate independent investigation into the tax affairs of the family of British prime minister 
        <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> (pictured).
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Ian_Cameron_(stockbroker)" title="Ian Cameron (stockbroker)" class="mw-redirect">Ian Cameron</a>, the late father of <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">UK Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, ran an offshore fund through Mossack Fonseca that avoided British taxes for thirty years. Residents of the Bahamas, including a part-time bishop, signed the paperwork.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> His company, Blairmore Holdings, moved to <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>, another country known for its lenient tax rules,<sup id="cite_ref-Tel_Ireland_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tel_Ireland-189">[189]</a></sup> in either 2010<sup id="cite_ref-Tel_Ireland_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tel_Ireland-189">[189]</a></sup> or 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Ireland_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Ireland-190">[190]</a></sup> because its directors believed it would "come under more scrutiny" after the younger Cameron became Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-Tel_Ireland_189-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tel_Ireland-189">[189]</a></sup> In response to his late father's inclusion on the firm's list of clients, David Cameron initially said his family's taxes were "a private matter"<sup id="cite_ref-campri_64-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campri-64">[64]</a></sup> but later issued a statement saying that he, his wife and children receive no benefit from the company, Blairmore Holdings, which is still in operation and has assets of £35 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Tel_Ireland_189-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tel_Ireland-189">[189]</a></sup> Cameron inherited £300,000 after his father died in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-campri_64-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campri-64">[64]</a></sup> On April 6, Cameron admitted that he had owned shares in Blairmore<sup id="cite_ref-GuardAdmit_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardAdmit-191">[191]</a></sup> and sold his shares before becoming PM; he paid tax on the dividends which he received from it, but there was no capital gains tax payable.<sup id="cite_ref-GuardAdmit_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardAdmit-191">[191]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Also included among the documents are the names of six members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>, several of whom have been donors to Cameron's Conservative Party.<sup id="cite_ref-another_Guardian_ref_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-another_Guardian_ref-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Tory_donors_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Tory_donors-193">[193]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Prominent members of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> criticized the involvement of the Cameron family in the scandal. <a href="/wiki/Shadow_Secretary_of_State_for_International_Development" title="Shadow Secretary of State for International Development">Shadow Secretary of State for International Development</a> <a href="/wiki/Diane_Abbott" title="Diane Abbott">Diane Abbott</a> described the revelations as "the tip of the iceberg" and "a stitch up", and urged "meaningful reform" of the UK tax authority, <a href="/wiki/HMRC" title="HMRC" class="mw-redirect">HMRC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Abbott_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abbott-194">[194]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Shadow_Chancellor_of_the_Exchequer" title="Shadow Chancellor of the Exchequer">Shadow Chancellor of the Exchequer</a> <a href="/wiki/John_McDonnell_(politician)" title="John McDonnell (politician)">John McDonnell</a> condemned the tax avoidance schemes as "immoral"<sup id="cite_ref-MSAbbott_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSAbbott-195">[195]</a></sup> and described the allegations as "extremely serious", saying "HMRC should treat this with utmost priority and urgently launch investigation".<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(United_Kingdom)" title="Leader of the Opposition (United Kingdom)">Leader of the Opposition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a>, urged an immediate independent investigation into the tax affairs of the Prime Minister's family, as well as tighter laws on <a href="/wiki/Tax_avoidance_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Tax avoidance in the United Kingdom" class="mw-redirect">UK tax avoidance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats" title="Liberal Democrats">Liberal Democrat</a> Home Office Minister <a href="/wiki/Norman_Baker" title="Norman Baker">Norman Baker</a> calling for further investigation of David Cameron's activities.<sup id="cite_ref-CameronResignRT_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CameronResignRT-198">[198]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> leader Nicola Sturgeon also called for a clampdown on UK tax avoidance which "stamps out this sort of behavour" and called for "utter transparency" from David Cameron, adding that "what shocks people most about some of this is that it is not illegal".<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Calls were made for the Prime Minister's resignation, especially after he admitted owning shares in his father's offshore company.<sup id="cite_ref-SparrowApril8_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SparrowApril8-200">[200]</a></sup> Describing Prime Minister David Cameron as the "most hypocritical prime minister of my lifetime", former <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_London" title="Mayor of London">Mayor of London</a> <a href="/wiki/Ken_Livingstone" title="Ken Livingstone">Ken Livingstone</a> said that "he shouldn't just resign, he should be sent to prison".<sup id="cite_ref-RTLivingstone_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RTLivingstone-201">[201]</a></sup> Former leader of the SNP <a href="/wiki/Alex_Salmond" title="Alex Salmond">Alex Salmond</a> also accused Cameron of "misleading the public" but said that "I'm not calling for his resignation until I get answers" to Cameron not registering offshore investment funds while an MP.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>As the United Kingdom still exercises varying degrees of control over <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a> which make up a large number of the many tax havens and 'secrecy jurisdictions' that exist, pressure has mounted on Prime Minister David Cameron to make changes.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJMacdonaldGross_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJMacdonaldGross-203">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Journal" title="Wall Street Journal" class="mw-redirect">Wall Street Journal</a></i>, the Panama Papers "are shining a light on the constellation of offshore centers in the last remnants of the British Empire, from <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> to the British Virgin Islands."<sup id="cite_ref-WSJMacdonaldGross_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJMacdonaldGross-203">[203]</a></sup> Of the companies handled by Mossack Fonseca which were included in the leaked data, British Overseas Territory the BVI topped the list, with 113,000 of the nearly 215,000 companies that Mossack Fonseca managed incorporated there. British Overseas Territory <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a> was 7th on the list.<sup id="cite_ref-Statista_chart_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statista_chart-205">[205]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Anti-David_Cameron_protest_04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Anti-David_Cameron_protest_04.jpg/250px-Anti-David_Cameron_protest_04.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Anti-David_Cameron_protest_04.jpg/375px-Anti-David_Cameron_protest_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Anti-David_Cameron_protest_04.jpg/500px-Anti-David_Cameron_protest_04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Anti-David_Cameron_protest_04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Protesters outside 
        <a href="/wiki/10_Downing_Street" title="10 Downing Street">10 Downing Street</a> call for David Cameron's resignation, 9 April 2016
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Cameron criticized complex offshore structures in 2012, saying that it is "not fair and not right", while at the <a href="/wiki/G8" title="G8" class="mw-redirect">G8</a> summit in 2013 he demanded more transparency, saying that it would be better for business.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Tory_donors_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Tory_donors-193">[193]</a></sup> In 2014, Cameron asked all Overseas Territories and Crown dependencies to set-up an open register of firms and individuals with investments registered in their jurisdictions, but by the time of the Panama Papers leak in April 2016, only Montserrat and Gibraltar had agreed to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-Soaraway_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soaraway-206">[206]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Leader of the Opposition Jeremy Corbyn, said "The government needs to stop pussyfooting around on tax dodging"<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> and called for "direct rule" to be imposed over British Overseas Territories and Crown dependencies that act as tax havens,<sup id="cite_ref-Indie_Corbyn_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Indie_Corbyn-208">[208]</a></sup> a move former Business Secretary <a href="/wiki/Vince_Cable" title="Vince Cable">Vince Cable</a> agreed with, although former attorney general <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Grieve" title="Dominic Grieve">Dominic Grieve</a> described it as a "bit of a nuclear option"<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> which would "destroy the livelihoods" of BVI inhabitants in the finance industry.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> The Labour Party also said that Cameron's plans for an "anti-corruption" summit in May<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> would be "a charade" if Cameron, as <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">chair</a> of the summit, did not require representatives of all Crown dependencies and overseas territories to attend.<sup id="cite_ref-MSAbbott_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSAbbott-195">[195]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Jennie Granger, a spokeswoman for HMRC said that the department had received "a great deal of information on offshore companies, including in Panama, from a wide range of sources, which is currently the subject of intensive investigation".
