She said HMRC had asked ICIJ to share all its data.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC:_reveal_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_reveal-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ITVApr416_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ITVApr416-212">[212]</a></sup> UK media<sup id="cite_ref-P_Eye_Troup_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-P_Eye_Troup-213">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Troup_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Troup-214">[214]</a></sup> revealed that <a href="/wiki/Edward_Troup" title="Edward Troup">Edward Troup</a>, appointed executive chair of HMRC in April 2016, was a former partner with <a href="/wiki/Simmons_%26_Simmons" title="Simmons &amp; Simmons">Simmons &amp; Simmons</a>, the London-based legal firm whose clients included the Panama-registered fund created by David Camerons father, Blairmore Holdings.<sup id="cite_ref-P_Eye_Troup_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-P_Eye_Troup-213">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Troup_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Troup-214">[214]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/The_McClatchy_Company" title="The McClatchy Company">McClatchy Newspapers</a>, the only participating US news organization, has found four Americans in the documents, all of whom were previously either accused or convicted of financial crimes such as fraud and tax evasion.<sup id="cite_ref-SeattleUS_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SeattleUS-44">[44]</a></sup> In 2008, Mossack Fonseca reportedly utilized a 90-year-old British man to conceal the offshore accounts of <a href="/wiki/Marianna_Olszewski" title="Marianna Olszewski">Marianna Olszewski</a>, a well-known US businesswoman.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCPanama_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCPanama-215">[215]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The lack of Americans in the leak has been suggested to be due to the facts that: shell companies can be created in the United States, major international banks based in America tend to have offshore accounts in the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> and US laws like the Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act (FATCA) and other cross-border initiatives had meant that the "tax evasion game [was] principally over for American taxpayers."<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In response to the lack of American individuals in the documents, the editor of <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCddeutsche_Zeitung" title="Süddeutsche Zeitung">Süddeutsche Zeitung</a></i> said: "Just wait for what is coming next."<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>United States president <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> addressed the leak during a press conference and said: "It's not that they're breaking the laws, it's that the laws are so poorly designed that they allow people, if they've got enough lawyers and enough accountants, to wiggle out of responsibilities that ordinary citizens are having to abide by."<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Some have argued that the <a href="/wiki/Panama%E2%80%93United_States_Trade_Promotion_Agreement" title="PanamaUnited States Trade Promotion Agreement">Panama Free Trade Agreement</a> supposedly allowed and made the abuses documented in the Panama Papers worse. This agreement was supported by President Barack Obama and former Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> However, according to Eoin Higgins and the <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i>, the Panama Free Trade Agreement actually forced Panama to release to the American regulatory authorities information on "the ownership of companies, partnerships, trusts, foundations, and other persons" which is why so few Americans' names are presented in the papers. Higgins stated "If Panama had ever been an attractive destination for American offshore storage of funds, this agreement shut the door on that possibility."<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Torneos &amp; Traffic (T&amp;T) is a subsidiary of Fox International Channels since 2005<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> (with investments since 2002) is the same company involved in corrupt practices in the acquisition of rights to major South American soccer tournaments.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panama_Papers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
